A copy of the original letter is sent for information.

Obstacles to Hunan Rice Exports 111

Additional Taxes Arouse Repercussions

The Hunan provincial authorities previously announced that the ban on Hunan rice exports would be lifted on the 22nd of this month. Therefore, Shanghai rice merchants prepared to go to Hunan for purchases, but unexpectedly encountered obstacles. The reasons for this are described in detail below.

Additional Taxes Suspended: The Hunan government had previously announced the regulations for rice transport passport fees, notifying the rice industry to take note. However, after the ban lifting order was announced on the 22nd, the provincial authorities announced that an additional special tax would be levied on exported rice to supplement government expenses. Rice merchants in Changsha unanimously opposed this. According to yesterday's telegram, the rice merchants have agreed to stop applying. Those who have already purchased rice but have not yet shipped it will also stop loading if the provincial authorities order them to pay the rice tax. The rice merchants are resisting the rice tax with a passive attitude. If it is not canceled, they will refrain from doing business, rendering the ban lifting order ineffective.

No Rice Loaded for Shanghai: After the order to lift the ban on rice exports in Hunan was announced, various shipping companies competed to send ships to Hunan in an effort to transport this rice to Shanghai. Unexpectedly, the additional tax caused an unforeseen event. Yesterday, various shipping companies in this city received telegrams from Hunan stating that ships that had arrived in Changsha had no rice to load because the rice merchants refused to pay the tax. This matter has not been resolved. The shipping lines in Hunan are diverting to transporting soybeans to Shanghai because there is a large stockpile of soybeans in Changsha, while the export of rice is temporarily hopeless.

Setbacks in the Resumption of Navigation on the Upper Yangtze 112

After the resumption of navigation on the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, the Shanghai-Hunan shipping companies unexpectedly encountered setbacks yesterday due to the postponement of cargo transportation. What we have heard is recorded as follows:

First Batch of Goods to Hunan Postponed: Hunan Changsha shipping companies reported loading a large batch of foreign miscellaneous goods, textiles, cotton yarn, sugar, etc., with the first batch shipped directly from Shanghai amounting to 2,000 tons. Because they had to arrive in Hunan by the end of this month, the shipping companies were approved to use the British Taikoo company's "Xiangtan" ship for transportation. It was originally scheduled to depart this morning, and customs clearance procedures were being processed. Suddenly, a urgent telegram arrived from Changsha, instructing to postpone the direct shipment of this large batch of goods. Yesterday, the shipping companies notified Taikoo, and the departure of "Xiangtan" to Changsha was also temporarily suspended.

Chinese Ships Also Stop Navigating Upstream: Sanbei company's "Hongheng" and "Hongyuan" ships were originally dedicated to the Changsha route. This time, "Hongheng" arrived in Shanghai and had its rudder repaired. It was scheduled to depart on the 28th and originally planned to go directly to Hunan. Yesterday, they received a telegram from Hankou stating that the water level in the upper reaches of the river had dropped significantly. If the ship were to enter Hunan, cargo may be in danger. For the sake of safe navigation and passengers and cargo, the company changed its route to Hankou. They also notified the shipping companies not to load goods directly to Changsha. At the same time, they also telegraphed the "Hongyuan" ship upstream to switch to the downstream route.

Japanese Ships Stopped Commercial Services First: Nisshin company's "Yuanjiang" ship has suspended its Changsha service and is transporting Japanese residents to Hankou.

Shanghai 113

Statement from the Water Company

Reasons for Appropriately Increasing Water Prices

The Shanghai Water Company of the Public Concession issued a statement yesterday, stating that there has been criticism from the outside about the increase in water prices. To avoid misunderstandings, the following statement is made: The company's dividends have been stipulated in a contract with the Public Works Department. The current price increase is not intended to increase dividends. Furthermore, the water price standard has never been as high as 10% or 12%. The current rate for residential water use is 6% of the rent, and after the price increase, it will be only 7.5%. This shows that the impact on individual rent is minimal. This water price has no relation to the amount of water used and cannot be said to restrict people's water use or deprive them of their drinking needs. Other water prices are also increased in the same proportion. This price increase was approved by the Sino-foreign board of directors after the Public Works Department sent personnel to inspect the accounts. The company's ability to supply drinking water has always been recognized by citizens. In order to maintain its effectiveness, it is necessary to increase expenses. This increase in expenses is entirely due to the sharp drop in the price of silver.

Revised Handling of Sino-Foreign Lawsuits 114

First Instance Cases of Sino-Foreign Lawsuits

Will Be Tried by the County Starting Next Month

After the abolition of the Commissioners for Foreign Affairs in various provinces, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has stipulated the procedures for handling Sino-foreign lawsuits. All Sino-foreign appeal cases accepted by the Commissioner's Office that have not been concluded will be handled by the High Courts or Branch Courts of various provinces in accordance with ordinary litigation procedures. The Judicial Yuan believes that there should be some supplementation regarding the previous method because some appeal cases in accordance with ordinary laws should be accepted by the District Court. After consulting with the Judicial Yuan, two revised methods have been established, which will be promulgated by the Judicial Yuan to the courts of various provinces for compliance and notified by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to the ministers of various countries for reference. The revised methods are as follows: (1) All appeal cases of Sino-foreign lawsuits that have been accepted and not concluded before the abolition of the Commissioner's Office shall be handled by the High Court or its Branch Court (After the District Court or its Branch Court renders a judgment on an appeal case of first instance, another appeal may be made to the Supreme Court). Sino-foreign lawsuits after the abolition shall be handled in accordance with the usual procedures. However, if preliminary jurisdiction over Sino-foreign appeal cases was exercised by the High Court or its Branch Court before this order arrived, the High Court or its Branch Court shall continue to handle them. (2) For first instance cases of Sino-foreign lawsuits, starting from September 1, 1919, all counties that do not concurrently administer justice shall be handled by the competent court (District Courts and their Branch Courts, local divisions or county courts that are attached to them, and counties that concurrently administer justice shall continue to be handled by the county magistrate for the time being). However, in civil cases, with the consent of both parties, they may request the court to accept the case in accordance with the regulations of consensual jurisdiction in the Revised Civil Procedure Law.

Chief of Section of Japanese Foreign Ministry Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday 115

Related to the Issue of the Japanese Minister to China

The Guowen News Agency reports that Mr. Tani Masayuki, Chief of the First Section of the Asian Bureau of the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs, who was specially dispatched to Shanghai by the Japanese government, arrived in Shanghai yesterday on the Nagasaki Maru postal ship. Shigemitsu Aoi, the acting Japanese minister in Shanghai, and other important officials and gentry greeted him at the port. After landing, Chief Tani went by car with Shigemitsu to the Japanese Consulate and held a closed-door meeting with Mr. Shigemitsu for two hours before leaving for the Wansui Pavilion for rest. That night, he took a night train to Beijing to meet with Consul Kamimura in Beijing to discuss important matters. When he arrived in Shanghai, Chinese and Japanese reporters boarded the ship for a short conversation, asking about the mission of his visit to China. Chief Tani refused to announce it, saying that it was confidential. However, he stated that matters concerning the Changqiu case, etc., were the responsibility of Chief Sangashima of the Second Section. Therefore, his visit to China was not for this matter. However, according to Japanese sources, Tani Masayuki's visit to Shanghai was indeed with an important mission, which was related to the changing of the Japanese minister to China. The Japanese government had previously planned to transfer Acting Minister Shigemitsu to the position of Director of the Asian Bureau and appoint a new minister to China. Because there had been no prior consultations, misunderstandings arose after the news was released, leading to a deadlock that has not been implemented to this day. Therefore, Chief Tani was specially sent to Shanghai to meet with Acting Minister Shigemitsu to explain everything and exchange opinions. Mr. Tani is now scheduled to take the liaison ship back to his country tomorrow (28th) to report on his mission. It is expected that there will be new news about the practical solution to the issue of the Japanese minister to China.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce 116

Investigating Dismissal Customs in Various Industries

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to various trade associations to investigate the dismissal dates of old customs in various industries in the city and to formulate measures for implementing the Gregorian calendar. The letter stated, "On the 25th of this month, the Social Affairs Bureau ordered an investigation into the admission and dismissal of employees in stores, which are temporarily handled in accordance with the old customs of various industries and changed to the Gregorian calendar. This Bureau has already announced it in Announcement No. 146. The dismissal dates of old customs in various industries in this city are inconsistent, some based on the peak and off-seasons of business, and some based on accounting dates. Each has its own reasons and can be followed as a custom. After changing to the Gregorian calendar, whether there will be any obstacles should be investigated in detail for review and approval. You are hereby ordered to comply and promptly and thoroughly investigate the dismissal dates of old customs in various industries in this city and formulate measures for implementing the Gregorian calendar and report for verification." Because the dismissal dates of employees in various industries are different, it is necessary to investigate and then summarize and consider measures. A letter is sent in advance for notification. Please investigate and reply in detail within five days of receiving the letter, stating the dismissal date stipulated in the customs of your industry, for the purpose of compiling and considering measures. This is very important.

Two Railroads 117

Hope for Resolution of Rice Subsidy Issue

Employees of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railroads with salaries above 50 yuan were facing difficulty in maintaining their livelihoods due to the soaring rice prices. Representatives were elected by the workers of the Wusong Machine Factory to petition the railroad bureau, requesting rice and housing subsidies. Liu Weizhi, Director of the Business Department of the Ministry of Railways and concurrently in charge of affairs of the two railroads, met with them and agreed to request the Ministry to act as an agent. The Ministry of Railways approved a rice subsidy of one yuan for those with salaries above 30 yuan. The workers felt that the amount was too small and insufficient, and continued to elect representatives to request again. Director Liu agreed to ask the Ministry again. It was said that the Ministry of Railways believed that the railroad bureau's income was not as good as before, and if further additions were made without end, the railroad was in danger of bankruptcy. Therefore, the request to the Ministry was made repeatedly. The Ministry approved yesterday to grant a rice subsidy of one and a half yuan to those with salaries above 30 yuan, and a subsidy of one yuan to those with salaries above 50 yuan. According to investigations, although this rice subsidy is small, it requires an additional budget of more than 100,000 yuan per year for the railroad bureau.

Prohibition of Soldiers Riding Trains Without Tickets 118

Proclamation of the Garrison Headquarters

The Songhu Garrison Headquarters issued a proclamation yesterday, stating, "For the sake of proclamation, transportation on the two railroads is extremely important, and all soldiers traveling must abide by discipline. In recent months, there have often been wounded soldiers without tickets, infringing on seats, which disrupts regulations and not only hinders railroad administration, but also tarnishes the reputation of the military. An order has been issued to the railroad bureau to add a third-class train car specifically for wounded soldiers, and all units, rear hospitals, railroad guard conscripts, and military police are to comply, strictly investigate, and specially issue this earnest proclamation. Hereafter, no matter what kind of soldiers are traveling, if they rely on their strength and act recklessly, and the above-mentioned situation occurs again, once discovered, they will be severely punished without leniency."

Baoshan County Held a County Administration Meeting Yesterday 122

Baoshan County Magistrate Qiu Mingjiu convened a county administration meeting yesterday morning at 10:00 AM in the west conference hall of the county government, attended by the heads of various bureaus under his jurisdiction, including Shen Jing, Qian Tianpeng, Wu Jietai, Pu Wengui, Wang Tongchuan, Yin Xiangsun, Xue Ying, Ji Zhonghe, Xu Liangxi, Ling Bin, and Shu Mengyuan. Magistrate Qiu, serving as chairman, reported on the following matters: The government previously used 140 yuan from the variable expenses of the First District Office for the repair of the county government's main hall and leaking roofs inside the building. The project is now completed, totaling 164.24 yuan. As the funds are local, a detailed report of the actual expenditure should be presented for public review and verification. Discussion items included: (1) After the stone bridge outside the South Gate was collapsed by military factory vehicles carrying cannons, this government sent a letter urging its prompt repair. On the 23rd (Saturday), the military factory sent engineer Zhang Deqing to survey the site, planning to use a steel bridge from the Railway Bureau for the reconstruction. The military factory would bear the cost. However, the two bridge abutments need to be widened by about one foot each and reinforced with cement to make the steel bridge surface more robust. The military factory intends to request Baoshan County to bear the cost of rebuilding these bridge abutments. Please decide on the matter. (Decision) The county government should instruct the Construction Bureau to send personnel to directly liaise with engineer Zhang Deqing of the military factory for detailed discussions, and then estimate the cost of rebuilding the two bridge abutments for further review. (2) The city wall near the South Gate has been significantly damaged by various public and private constructions, with many city bricks removed. As the South Gate is the only major gate in Baoshan, this is unsightly. Should the dismantling be prohibited, or to what extent should it be restricted to avoid hindering both public and private construction and local aesthetics? Please decide on the matter. (Decision) The Construction Bureau and the Education Bureau are responsible for preliminary planning and arrangement. The county government should issue a public notice prohibiting further random dismantling. (3) The stone suspension bridge outside the North Gate is showing signs of damage again. Should the passage of heavy vehicles be restricted? (Decision) The Construction and Public Security Bureau should jointly stipulate the weight of vehicles allowed to pass and post a notice to enforce the restriction. (4) Farm Director Li Zhonghe proposed that the issue of rickshaw license fees in Shishan County had been approved by the previous County Magistrate Wu at the county administration meeting, and a collection method was submitted to the authorities for approval. However, it has not been effectively implemented. Please decide on a solution. (Decision) The county government should investigate the case and order the relevant bureau to implement it effectively.

Court Changes Office Hours 123

Changes in Prosecutors

This port's procuratorate, to facilitate litigation, only conducted business in the mornings during July and August, as previously reported. Now that the summer break is over, Chief Prosecutor Liu plans to resume the original schedule, from 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM, and from 1:00 PM to 5:00 PM in the afternoons, effective September 1st. It is also heard that there have been some changes among the prosecutors. Liu Pingfan and Xu Heling have been transferred to Anhui and Jiangxi, respectively, and their vacancies will be filled by Yang Qi and Wu Shixin. Yang is a graduate of a Belgian university and has conducted extensive research in criminal law and criminology. He has just returned after graduation. Wu has been transferred from Hubei. It is further heard that Chief Prosecutor Liu, due to the heavy workload and small staff of the procuratorate, and to implement streamlining measures, plans to add a candidate prosecutor. The most promising candidate is the chief secretary, Chen Lian, a graduate of a law school who has served as a prosecutor in various places and enjoys a good reputation in the judicial circle.

Letter Requesting the Use of Domestic Paper 125

Zheng Shouzhi's Reply to the Shanghai All-Circles Relief and慰勞 Association

The Shanghai All-Circles Fundraising Association for Disaster Relief for War-Affected Areas and慰勞 Frontline Soldiers sent out notices, regulations, and donation booklets to solicit support from all sectors in order to actively carry out disaster relief and慰勞. Zheng Shouzhi, in addition to replying with a letter agreeing to do his best to raise donations, made many comments on the matter of using suitable domestic paper for such printed materials. The original letter is recorded as follows: "In response, I have received your letter, along with temporary receipts and donation booklets. I am deeply moved by the compassion of you gentlemen for the wounded and devastated, your concern for the border, your joy in remembering suffering, and your ability to think of danger in times of peace. I, Shouzhi, am not talented, but I dare not fail to follow in the footsteps of you gentlemen, to contribute my modest efforts to fulfill the duty of a citizen. I will wait until I have collected a considerable amount before presenting it. However, I have noticed that the donation booklets, donation notices, brochures, and receipts used by your association are all Daolin paper imported from abroad. This may be a temporary oversight or carelessness, and not a deliberate intention. However, considering the patriotic and philanthropic enthusiasm of your association, such an omission is regrettable. Nowadays, our countrymen are vigilant about the danger of economic aggression by imperialists, and the national goods movement is spreading throughout the country. Machine-made improved domestic paper products are gradually increasing. For example, the Lian Shi, Mao Bian, and Hai Yue paper produced by the Jiangnan Paper Company are even superior to those imported from the East. Among them, the Hai Yue paper is particularly suitable for such printed materials due to its soft, tough, and smooth texture. However, it is often seen that various sectors, when publishing printed materials, often abandon suitable domestic paper and do not use it, as if foreign goods are necessary to meet their needs. What is the purpose of this? It is simply due to a momentary oversight and failure to examine habitual practices, which contradicts their usual aspirations. They do not realize that small leaks, if not stopped, will become rivers and oceans, and great wastes result from small drops. The decline of our national livelihood and the decay of industry are rooted in this subtle negligence. It is hoped that we will thoroughly awaken, take practical steps, act diligently, not make empty statements to seek fame, and not neglect small acts of goodness. This will enable national goods to be gradually promoted and foreign goods to be rejected without explicit resistance. Our country's economic future may then have a chance. I offer these thoughts for your consideration, hoping that they are not contrary to the patriotic and philanthropic enthusiasm of you gentlemen. Respectfully addressed to the Shanghai All-Circles Fundraising Association for Disaster Relief for War-Affected Areas and慰勞 Frontline Soldiers."

The Relief Committee Dispatches Personnel for Relief

The recent sudden war in Qufu County, Shandong Province, has caused the destruction of cultural relics in forests and temples. The commercial markets, properties, and houses in the area have suffered significant losses due to artillery fire. The number of casualties is countless. The Qufu Chamber of Commerce and various organizations previously telegraphed the Relief Committee, requesting prompt assistance. Chairman Xu Jingren presented a request to the government and the院 for appropriation of funds. He also consulted with Committee Member Wang Yiting of the Shanghai Office to publish advertisements soliciting emergency relief donations. He also telegraphed the Qufu Comfort Committee, requesting them to investigate the disaster situation to facilitate appropriate action. Yesterday, a reply telegram was received stating that the disaster in the county was extremely severe. Chairman Xu has now appointed a special commissioner to carry funds for distribution immediately, and telegraphed Wang Yiting to find ways to raise additional relief funds to avoid exhausting resources. He also requested the China济生会 to allocate various types of epidemic prevention medicines for distribution. Wang is currently soliciting donations from various sources. If any enthusiastic philanthropists wish to provide emergency relief to Qufu, please send donations to the Renji Hall内, the Shanghai Office of the Relief Committee, as soon as possible. This is truly providing assistance when it is most needed.

Route Massenet 129

A Bandit Killed

After Robbing in the French Concession, the Bandit Fled into Route Massenet

One Bandit Killed on the Spot, Another Captured Alive

The Police Fired, Wounding Two Pedestrians

Around 1:15 PM yesterday afternoon, a bandit was killed on Route Massenet in the Public Concession. This bandit had robbed on Route Pelles in the French Concession, crossed Avenue Edward VII, and fled into Route Massenet, where he was shot and killed by pursuing police. Another accomplice was also captured. When the police fired, stray bullets hit a rickshaw puller and a laborer, respectively. The details are as follows:

Robbery in the French Concession Anhui native Fang Lizhi, 46 years 130

old, had a career in government service and now resides at No. 7 Lihe Lane, Route Pelles, French Concession. Around 1:00 PM yesterday afternoon, two bandits suddenly broke into his home, robbing clothing, jewelry, and silver dollars worth about 20 yuan before fleeing. The victim chased after them, shouting for help.

Fleeing into Route Massenet The two bandits went south from Lihe Lane 131

to Avenue Dubail, turned east towards Rue de la Porte Blanche, where one bandit was captured. The other bandit went west and then north, crossed Avenue Edward VII, and fled into Route Massenet in the Public Concession. Seeing a rickshaw, he jumped on and tried to escape.

One Bandit Killed As the bandit crossed Avenue Foch to 132

Route Massenet, five or six officers from the Xinzha Police Station were already alerted and pursued him. The bandit, in desperation, fired his gun to resist arrest. The police returned fire, and the bandit was fatally shot in the chest, abdomen, legs, and back, succumbing to eight gunshot wounds.

Two Pedestrians Hit by Stray Bullets Rickshaw puller Xia Guangxing, 133

from Jiangbei, 28 years old, was shot in the right leg. Laborer Zhang Gaogui, 32 years old, from Jiangbei, was shot in the waist. Both were sent to Renji Hospital for treatment by the police. Their injuries are serious.

Bandit's Corpse Inspected The captured bandit was found to be carrying 134

two pistols, one four inches and one six inches long, which were taken to the French Police Station for safekeeping. The bandit's corpse was taken to the Tongren輔元堂驗屍所. At 3:00 PM, Zhu, the judge of the criminal division of the French Court, arrived at the morgue to examine the body, after being informed of the situation by the detectives. Zhu ruled that the deceased, an unnamed bandit, had died from gunshot wounds sustained while resisting arrest. He ordered that photographs be taken and that the Tongren Auxiliary Yuantang provide a coffin for burial.

Three Ships Salvaging the Kangtai Sank 135

Three Ships Sank in the Wind

All Nineteen People Fell into the Water

Survived Because of Their Good Swimming Skills

The Japanese company contracted by San Bing 洋行 of this port to salvage the Kang Qin sunken ship has been working since the start of the salvage, which is more than a month. The ship's machinery, boilers, and various engines have already been salvaged one after another. However, the hull is deeply embedded in the riverbed, making it difficult to retrieve. The Japanese used 1,000 pounds of dynamite for underwater blasting, causing the ship's bottom to break open and the wood to float. At that time, they hired two civilian boats (small traveling wind boats) to retrieve the wood. Unexpectedly, the Japanese ordered two wind boats, named "Mada Ahui", to be towed by their own chemical small wheel on the previous day. When they were salvaging the wood, suddenly at about 8 o'clock in the evening, a storm broke out, causing the chemical small wheel and the two wind boats to be difficult to support. Then they all capsized, and a total of nineteen boatmen and sailors on the three ships all fell into the water and drifted away. Fortunately, all the people knew the art of swimming. At that time, everyone used their strength to fight the waves and swim on the sea to escape from danger and not be with the wave officials. Subsequently, the salvage office of the bank learned of the news of the salvage office and immediately drove to the rescue and rescued all the people on the water. Among them, several people such as Zhang of the Fengfeng boat were either too frightened or because their bodies were concerned. They were unconscious and had cold limbs when rescued. After being rescued one by one, all the people who fell into the water were restored to their lives. The Mada Ahui chemical small wheel and a wind boat sank without a trace at the time. There is still a wind boat, although it was damaged by the storm and the giant waves, but because the rescue of the small fire wheel of Ruifeng was quick, the broken ship was towed to the stone embankment at that time, but the wind and waves were even more violent at night, resulting in the broken ship still sunk. It is heard that the bank lost more than a thousand taels this time, and the boss of the Mada Ahui medicine wheel, Tan Axi, lost even more.

Monstrous Fetus of a Woman 136

One Son with Three Mouths

Shrunken Head, Fangs, Half a Leg

Li Xuehao from Yancheng, who lives at No. 1, Hong'an Lane, Hanzhong Road, Zhabei, is a stone mason at the ferry crossing of Binlang Road in the Public Concession, leaving early and returning late. His wife, Ms. Yan, is 36 years old and works hard at home. She has already given birth to three sons. Last year, during the remaining days of winter, the wife became pregnant. At 11:00 PM on the previous day (the 25th), it was time for her to give birth, but unexpectedly, she gave birth to a monstrous fetus, which was immediately thrown into the trash can at the entrance of the alley. When Xuehao sent the monster back, he was followed by a black cat. When he arrived at the room, the cat suddenly disappeared. Looking at his wife again, her abdomen was still swollen. The monster that was newly born had a very long head at first. After landing, it suddenly shrank. Both hands were attached to the side of the body and were quite small. Both legs were also straight and short. The nose was flat, and there were two mouths. There was still a hole in the back of the head, appearing like three mouths. The two mouths in the front were arranged in a row and both had fangs. The mouth at the back was unique. When asked if it was male or female, it was not possible to tell. The next morning (that is, yesterday morning) at about 8:00 AM, neighbors flocked to the trash can to see it, and all were surprised.

A Prisoner Accuses the Gang Leader 137

Wang Ada, Whose Sentence Is About to Expire, Is Accused by Fellow Prisoners

Wang Ada from Ningbo conflicted with his fellow townsman Gu Baoxiang on Broadway Road on the 28th of last month, starting with an argument and then a fight. Gu was injured in the fight, and the Huishan Police Station detained Wang and sent him to the Special District Local Court, which sentenced him to 30 days of detention, to be served in the West Prison. His sentence would soon expire and he would be free. However, seven fellow prisoner thieves, Dai Anxiang, Shen Aqing, Yu Amao, Pan Meisheng, Shen Longyi, Zhang Acai, and Chen Acai, saw that Wang was in prison and confirmed that he was their leader. They feared that Wang would be released after his term expired and would remain at large. Therefore, they specifically accused him, saying that the pistols used by them when robbing merchants and residents of Xinjihang Road and Dongjiaxing Road were all supplied by Wang, and the stolen goods were also distributed by Wang. The western officer in charge of the prison reported this to his superiors. It was found that the seven thieves, including Dai, were arrested by Feng Zhiming, an investigator from the General Inspection Office of the General Patrol Room. In February of this year, the former Provisional Court sentenced them to 18 years of imprisonment each. Feng Investigator was ordered to bring Wang Ada back to the police station for investigation and prosecution. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Special District Local Court. Judge Ge opened the court for interrogation. Feng then brought Dai and others to the case for verification. According to Dai, Wang Ada was indeed the leader of the thieves, supplying pistols and distributing the stolen goods on the spot. After we were arrested, we concealed this situation during the trial because of Wang's instructions. At that time, Wang also promised to hire lawyers to defend us and find ways to rescue us, but later he failed to do so, etc. The other six, including Yu Amao, were very hesitant in their testimony. Judge Ge then ordered that the seven prisoners, including Dai, be sent back to the West Prison. Wang Ada was detained for further interrogation.

Lake Bandits Plunder Jinjiazhuang Shanghai News 138

Guowen News Agency reports that someone came to Shanghai from Zhujiajiao yesterday, talking about the looting of Jinjiazhuang, Dianshan Lake, in the southern township of Kunshan County. At 4:00 AM on the 25th of this month (the previous day), a large gang of bandit ships, totaling twenty-four, arrived. There were about two hundred bandits, all armed with long guns, who landed on the shore and searched houses one by one. They shot and killed Mr. Gu Da, a gentleman, on the spot, and robbed four long guns and one box cannon from the local self-defense team. They also kidnapped more than ten people, including Gu Shoude, Gu Yudong, Zhu Jinshou (over eighty years old), Zhu Aliang, the son of Li Cairu, and the mother of Hu Wenlan. At 9:00 AM, they assembled and left, having searched for four hours. No large or small household was spared. Subsequent investigations revealed that clothing, jewelry, silver dollars, and other items worth about 10,000 yuan were looted. Before leaving, the bandits threatened to return to loot again if the village did not hand over 150,000 silver dollars within four days.

US Court Tribunal Verdict 140

The Harbin Citibank Case

Return the Remaining Balance of the Harbin Electric Company's Deposit

The Great American Evening Post reports that the Harbin Electric Joint Stock Company sued the American Court Envoy Office in this port to order Citibank in Harbin to return the remaining balance of the deposit of Hada Yang 49,680.81 yuan. The American Envoy has ruled that Citibank should return the full amount to the plaintiff. It is reported that the entanglement in this case lies in the signature procedure. The Harbin Electric Company previously signed a contract with the American BKM Company to build a power plant and tram line, and deposited money in Citibank in Harbin to guarantee the payment of the goods when due, and agreed with the bank that the payment could only be made with the joint signatures of both parties. Later, the two parties disagreed on the issue of fulfilling the contract, and the BKM Company terminated the project and withdrew its representative stationed in Harbin. Both parties agreed that the contract was invalid, but the remaining balance of the deposit could not be paid due to the signature procedure, and therefore the lawsuit was filed in court.

Singapore 142

Negotiations on the Ban on Chinese Laborers

The Singapore colonial government announced on July 31 that Chinese laborers would be banned from landing on the Malay Peninsula for eight or nine months. It also announced that child laborers under the age of 14 would not be allowed to land during these three months. The Singapore Consul General Tang Liu telegraphed the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, requesting serious negotiations with the governments of these countries to avoid affecting the labor community. The Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee held that Singapore is the gateway to the Malay Peninsula and is not only the necessary transit point for overseas Chinese coming to the Malay Peninsula but also the hub of Euro-Asian transportation. Now that the ban on the entry of Chinese laborers has been announced, all adult Chinese laborers who have immigrated from China are calculated in Singapore. After calculation, they can transfer to Penang Island for landing. Laborers are not allowed to land in other ports besides Singapore Penang and 嶮. If the above methods are not followed, they will be arrested immediately. The Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee has received successive telegrams from overseas Chinese compatriots in Nanyang requesting relief. It is reported that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has been requested to negotiate a proper solution with the governments of these countries as soon as possible.

Yuanfang Road Fire 149

Sentencing Pending in Case of Four Deaths by Burning

Li Tianmin Insists on Being Out

Co-habitant Testifies He Was Home

Li Tianmin, a man from Chaozhou, allegedly started a fire at his residence at 133 Yuanfang Road on the 5th of this month at 3:00 AM while preparing opium, resulting in the death of four people. The police arrested Li and brought him to the Special District Court. After several investigations, as reported in this newspaper, the case was heard again yesterday. The police lawyer stated that after the last hearing, the police sent detectives back to the fire scene to investigate and recovered an iron box belonging to the defendant, but there were no prohibited items inside. A small jar of liquid was also presented as evidence, and the judge was asked to examine whether it was opium, as suspected, or oil, as the defendant claimed. Subsequently, a Mrs. Liu testified, stating that the defendant was her husband's younger brother, whose real name was Liu Juemin, and was a teacher in Nanyang. The house on Yuanfang Road was originally rented by her husband for many years. Initially, there was a school in the house, so her family moved to 917 Donghan Bili Road five years ago. The defendant returned to Shanghai this time and stayed in the wing room downstairs of that house. That night, the defendant suddenly came to her house and knocked on the door. She opened the door and let him in, and saw that he was naked, with only a sweat shirt covering his lower body. When she asked him what happened, she learned that he had encountered a fire. She immediately told him to go inside and put on clothes. The defendant said that there were still important items in his room and went back to retrieve them, but he did not return for a long time, and then learned that he had been arrested by the police. The back of the house's parlor was rented to Qian Liangen, who had not moved in for long. The residents upstairs were mostly from Jianghuai. The defendant would make opium in the kitchen, she claimed. Then, Mr. Mai Er, a Westerner from the Hongkou Fire Brigade, described the situation of driving to the scene to put out the fire that night, stating that after investigation, the fire started around the stairs in the house. Jiang Shaokuang, a Chinese staff member of the brigade, testified that after the fire was extinguished that night, two copper pots used for preparing opium were found, and the charcoal in the stove was still burning. Subsequently, Qian Liangen, Wang Jinkui, Tian Chenshi, and Xiao Wang, residents of the house, each described what they saw. Qian insisted that he was at a relative's house that night and did not come home, so how could it be said that the fire started in his room? Wang Jinkui and others all said that Qian was indeed at home that night and had an argument with the residents upstairs because the washing water leaked from the upstairs floor into Qian's room. The defendant also testified that the fire started in Qian's room, and he woke up from a dream and was arrested in the alley after escaping. Finally, the lawyers for both parties concluded their arguments, and the court ordered the defendant to be detained to await sentencing.

Government Salt Boat Damaged by Sand Dredger 150

Liu Shenglai, a fisherman from Daishan, Zhejiang, was transporting a boatload of government salt from Daiao to the Shanghai government salt depot. When he arrived at the Wusongkou the day before yesterday, Yu Xiasheng's sand dredger from Sijiao collided with the salt boat due to careless navigation. The tide immediately rushed in, wetting the government salt, resulting in a significant loss. Yu Xiasheng knew he was at fault after causing the accident, but claimed it was unintentional. In addition to hiring a boat to transport the remaining intact government salt to Shanghai for delivery, he also intended to plead with the depot to handle the matter lightly and exempt him from compensating for the losses.

Theft Discovered on Huangpu River 151

A Large Cable Leads to the Arrest

Zhang Yuting, a detective from the Shanghai Municipal Police Department's Water Patrol Team, was patrolling the Huangpu River near Zhangjiabang Pier in Pudong at about 4:00 AM yesterday when he found a suspicious客船. He boarded the boat to investigate and found a large cable in the boat, about eight inches in diameter and more than ten yards long. He asked the boatman what the cable was for. The boatman said it belonged to passengers Jin Akang, Wang Apin, and Gui Aquan. When questioned about the origin of the cable, Jin Akang and others hesitated, so all the people and evidence were taken to the team. During preliminary interrogation by Chief Xu, the boatwoman Wang Yangshi stated that the cable was transferred to her boat by Jin Akang and others from a coal boat. She said that Jin and others had previously hired her boat to transport ten barrels of paint and lead wire rope to the Laobaidu Pier in Puxi, and then Jin and others sold them all at the Kunhe Hardware Store, so they knew each other and she transported the cable for them, but she did not know where the cable came from. When questioned, Jin and others claimed that the cable was stolen from a certain ship in the Huangpu River and admitted to stealing paint and other items and selling them to the Kunhe Hardware Store. It was discovered that Jin Akang and others were habitual thieves, and the Kunhe Hardware Store specialized in receiving stolen goods, which was extremely abhorrent. The store owner, Gu Akun, was summoned to the case, and it was ordered to prepare a document and submit it to the Third Section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Ha San, from Jiangbei, was walking along East Huade Road at about 9:00 AM yesterday when he was hit by a Route 10 public bus. He was seriously injured and sent to Tongren Hospital, where he died in less than half an hour.

Two Workers Electrocuted 153

One Dead, One Critical

Zhou Zhongyuan and Liu Jinrong, workers in the grinding room of the Meisheng Machinery Iron Factory at 120 Dongyouheng Road, were walking past the entrance at about 10:00 AM yesterday when an electric wire suddenly fell from above, hitting Liu, who was immediately electrocuted and died. Zhou Zhongyuan was also shocked and fainted to the ground. He was rushed to Tongren Hospital, where his condition was critical. The deceased was 23 years old and from Jiangbei.

Thugs Rob and Injure Man 154

Li Defu, a 26-year-old man from Jiangbei, worked at the Hu Hongsheng Bowl Shop at the Old North Gate. The night before last, he accompanied his cousin Li Heshang back to his hometown. When they passed the Jinliyuan Pier in the French Concession, Li Heshang went to the public restroom to defecate. Li Defu was standing outside waiting with his bag of clothes when three or four thugs came up and tried to snatch the bag. Li resisted, and the thugs gathered to more than twenty people. Holding watermelon knives, they stabbed Li once in the abdomen, causing his intestines to protrude, and once in the right arm, causing very serious injuries. He went to Tongren Hospital for treatment. The thugs opened the stolen package and found only two sets of short shirts and pants, and nothing else of value, so they abandoned them on the ground and fled.

Debt Leads to Opium Suicide 155

The Impoverished Circumstances of Jiang Jiayun

Jiang Jiayun, a native of Wuxi, used to work in a rice shop in Wuxi. He resigned and came to Shanghai with his wife and three children in February, renting a house on Wuzhen Road in Zhabei. Jiang was recommended by a relative to work as a cargo manager at a foreign warehouse in Pudong. However, life in Shanghai was difficult, and his salary was not enough to cover expenses, resulting in two months of rent arrears. Recently, due to financial problems, the couple often quarreled. One Sunday, Jiang was resting at home when, for some reason, the couple quarreled again. At that time, his friend Li came to his house to ask for a loan. Jiang had no money to pay him and was ridiculed by Li. Jiang was very angry and, feeling embarrassed, decided to end his life. That night, he went to a certain opium den and bought half a yuan's worth of opium, brought it home, and swallowed it in the room. When the poison took effect in the middle of the night, he moaned incessantly. His wife noticed that his face had turned pale and rushed him to the hospital. According to the doctor, his life could be saved if there were no changes within 60 hours.

Driver Who Killed Someone in 156

Car Accident Awaits Sentencing

Liu Daoyou, a man from Jiangbei, made a living driving cars. Although his skills were not extremely bad, he was careless and drove arbitrarily fast. Recently, he was summoned by the Special District Court and fined ten yuan for disobeying a traffic police officer. However, not long after the punishment, he caused a major accident on the 23rd of this month at 3:00 PM, killing one person and injuring two others. At that time, Liu was driving a fully loaded truck with the number 16665 on Baker Road. On the sidewalk next to the road was an old woman from Yancheng, Chen Liu, who was sleeping there because of the heat. Liu suddenly drove onto the sidewalk, and the wheels crushed the old woman's head, waist, and back, killing her instantly. He continued to drive away quickly, causing two passing men to be knocked down. A bamboo fence next to the road was also crashed into a hole. The Chinese police officer No. 205 saw the scene, sent the two injured men and women to the morgue and hospital, respectively, and arrested Liu. The court examined the body and ordered it to be coffined. The police filed a public prosecution against Liu for causing death. Yesterday morning, Judge Ge Zhiqin proposed a trial. Chen Xiaolou, the son of the deceased, arrived in court and described the tragic death of his mother, requesting that the matter be handled strictly. However, the injuries of the two injured men were not fatal, and they had recovered in the hospital and returned to their hometown in Kunshan. According to police lawyer Zhang Tianyin, the defendant drove his car so carelessly and treated human life like a game, making it very unsafe for pedestrians. He requested a severe punishment to warn others. The defendant stated that at that time, someone suddenly ran out of an alley and crossed the road, and he wanted to avoid this person, so he drove the car to the side of the road, resulting in the accident, which was not intentional. After hearing the case, Judge Ge ordered Liu Daoyou to be detained to await sentencing.

Movie Actor's Home Robbed 157

One Thief and Stolen Goods Intercepted

Sentencing Postponed for Further Interrogation

Ren Yutian, who worked as a movie actor, lived at 1109 Xin Mali, Mahe Road. At about 8:00 AM the day before yesterday, Ren was still in bed when five robbers suddenly came in, each holding a pistol. They swarmed in, first driving Ren's five family members to a corner, ordering them to be silent, and then began to search and ransack, flipping over boxes and cabinets for a quarter of an hour, looting gold jewelry, clothing, and other items, and then fleeing out with a whoop. Ren's relative Shen Yugui arrived from outside, saw the situation, turned around and chased after them, shouting for thieves. The thieves, fearing that fleeing together would attract the attention of passersby and be intercepted, scattered and fled in different directions. One thief from Jianghuai, named Gu Zhenhua, did not hide his firearm, but held it in his hand and ran towards the concession. When he reached the corner of 246 Kaizier Road, Songshan Road, he was stopped by Shun Yizi and Liu Yushan. Gu was a gatekeeper hired by the resident of No. 246, and Liu was the resident's bodyguard. At that time, they were both enjoying the cool air in front of the door, and they saw Gu Zhenhua running wildly with a weapon in his hand. They suspected that he was not a good person, so they raised their pistols to stop him from moving forward. Gu knew that it was difficult to resist and surrendered. He was handed over to the nearby French police station. After interrogation by the police chief, it was found that the thief's gun had eight bullets, and four pieces of gold jewelry were found on his person. After a while, the Zhabei police station learned that a thief had been caught and sent detective Zhao Qingkui to cooperate with the Western detective to request the French police station to transfer him. Permission was granted. Gu Zhenhua, along with the pistol bullets and gold jewelry, was taken back together. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Special District Court, where Judge Sun Yuan opened the court for interrogation. After the police lawyer Wang Yaotang described the case, he requested a postponement because there were still accomplices at large, so that they could be tracked down. Ren Yutian, the victim, explained the situation of the robbery at that time, stating that the stolen property was worth more than 80 yuan, and the four pieces of gold jewelry recovered were indeed the stolen goods. When questioned, Gu Zhenhua directly admitted to forming a gang, holding weapons to rob and dividing the spoils, but said that the pistol he was holding belonged to a surname Ma, who was on the run. Judge Sun ordered Gu to be taken back to the police station for detention and adjourned the hearing to another date.

Zhu Afu Assassinated 158

Family Requests Exemption from Autopsy Granted

Zhu Afu, a 40-year-old man from Tongzhou who lived at 2054 and a half Shouren Lane, Gongping Road, Dongyouheng Road, in the Public Concession, worked for a certain company on Zilai Street in the French Concession. At 0:15 yesterday morning, he left the company to go home. Just as he left the alley, he was suddenly stabbed three times in the left chest, right shoulder, and right arm by an enemy using a sharp blade. The murderer fled after achieving his goal. Zhu was injured and went to the Da Ziminzhong Police Station and was transferred to Renji Hospital. He died at 9:30 AM due to excessive blood loss. The hospital notified the police station, who transported the body to the Tongren Fuyuantang morgue for an autopsy. Subsequently, the family submitted a request to the police station for exemption from the autopsy. The police chief approved it and ordered them to quickly collect the body for burial.

Agricultural Inspection Bureau 159

Explains Reasons for Inspecting Wheat

The Shanghai Agricultural Products Inspection Bureau of the Agricultural, Mining, and Industrial Bureau yesterday sent a letter to the Machinery Flour Mill Association explaining the inspection of wheat, stating that wheat is a major staple food, and in recent years, the sales of wheat in various ports have increased sharply. The practice of mixing cement and gravel has become increasingly serious, which not only hinders the hygiene of people's food, but also easily causes the quality to become moldy and rotten due to excessive water content. Mixing with gravel can easily damage the milling machine, and there is even a risk of fire. This causes great losses to manufacturers. As a result, the reputation of domestic wheat has gradually declined, and foreign wheat has taken the opportunity to enter the market, resulting in a huge outflow of money. This bureau is responsible for eliminating agricultural pests and is thinking about ways to improve the situation. It has now approved a letter from the Jiangsu Agricultural and Mining Department forwarded by the Shanghai Flour Industry Association, requesting strict prohibition of mixing cement and other substances into wheat. The bureau has reported this to the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining, ordering the Jiangbei Branch to first conduct trial inspections of wheat in the Jiangbei area, with the aim of gradually promoting it. Since the Jiangbei Branch began implementing the inspection, it believes that the results are still good, and it is beneficial to both the hygiene of people's food and the interests of manufacturers. However, it has received a letter from your association, stating that there are still four points that are not clear about the trial measures for inspecting wheat stipulated by this bureau. The following is a further explanation: (1) According to the general practice of inspecting agricultural products, it is carried out either at the time of import and export or at the time of transaction. It does not matter whether the cargo owner is a farmer or a merchant. According to the precedents of various countries, this is always the case. Moreover, the malpractices of mixing water and mud in wheat in our country are mostly caused by merchants and boatmen. Therefore, this bureau's inspection of wheat especially focuses on merchants and boatmen, which is the fundamental solution. (2) Shanghai is the center of the flour industry in the country, and Jiangbei is the most abundant wheat-producing area in our country. In addition to supplying some of the wheat produced to local flour mills, a large amount is also transported to Shanghai for sale. Since this bureau has a Jiangbei Branch, it should first order its implementation. Other places should be organized in order. It should be known that the national territory is very vast, and all administration can only be carried out gradually, and it is difficult to pass it all at once. (3) The trial measures for inspecting wheat stipulate the punishment of adulterated or counterfeit wheat, which is originally intended to ban through punishment and prevent unscrupulous merchants from following suit. It is clear that honest merchants will not engage in counterfeiting. However, this bureau cannot omit this article when formulating regulations to prevent unscrupulous people from knowingly violating them. It also deeply hopes that such facts will not be discovered, so that it is unnecessary to cite them as regulations, which will be of great benefit to the factory and will not be a hindrance. If the wheat transported by the factory is found to be unqualified and is indeed transported from elsewhere, and the situation is excusable, it should be ordered to find ways to improve it and purchase carefully in the future. If there is intentional violation, it should also be punished according to the regulations. National administration is to seek the interests of the public, and it is not convenient to condone a small number of people. (4)

This bureau handles the inspection administration in order to make up for the various facilities and procedural costs of implementing the inspection, and has to collect inspection fees. The nature of this fee is different from the special flour tax and wheat tax. According to the precedents of various countries, Japan, for example, charges each dan of wheat a fee of 4.5 to 8.9 points. However, the regulations of this bureau on the inspection of agricultural products stipulate that the inspection fee is only 2% of the value of the goods. Because this wheat inspection concerns the people's food and is a trial, it is especially considerate of the difficulties of merchants and the people, and has been approved by the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining to reduce the inspection fee to one cent per dan of wheat. According to the market price, it is less than two thousandths, which is very small and can only make up for the smallest part of the cost required to implement the inspection. Moreover, the wheat in our country is adulterated with water and mud, ranging from two or three catties to more than ten catties per dan. For example, if the factory purchases 1,000 dan of inferior goods, it will secretly lose 100 yuan. If it is inspected, the inferior goods will be eliminated, which can avoid secret consumption, and this small inspection fee seems to be the responsibility to bear. It is not like a special tax or wheat tax that can be compared. In summary, although the matter is a trial, the situation should be observed at any time and the regulations should be revised as appropriate to make it perfect. However, the four points raised in the letter feel that your association has not fully understood. The corresponding letter is replied, hoping that you will check it.

Proposal to Ban the Import of Japanese Cocoons 160

Gu Suming, a member of the Jiaxing Chamber of Commerce, believes that the huge import of Japanese cocoons has a great impact on agricultural products. He sent a letter to Wang Xiaolai, chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and Wang Yansong, a member of the Standing Committee, requesting that a proposal be submitted to find a way to stop it. The original letter stated that since countries such as France, Italy, and Japan suddenly rose to compete in the silk cocoon industry and surpassed China, foreign trade has fallen sharply, and there is almost no place for Chinese silk in the world market, which is heartbreaking to say. Fortunately, in recent years, the call for promoting domestic goods has been endless, and the improvement of silk fabrics has also made daily progress. Although it cannot win overseas, it can still continue to be held domestically. Unexpectedly, the alarming news came that a large number of Japanese dried cocoons were being transported to Shanghai for sale, which has become a reality. The first batch weighed 240,000 pounds, and after that, there will be a batch every seven days, with a total of 10,000 packages purchased. It will drive straight in, sell smoothly, and be seen rolling in, endlessly. Chinese silk cocoons will not only be rejected abroad, but will also be abandoned by the Chinese people. From then on, domestic cocoons will be equal to waste cotton, sericulture can be ignored, and national destruction and species extinction can be awaited. Japan takes China as its first economic invasion market in East Asia, and does everything possible. Taking advantage of the weakness of China's productivity and the weakness of merchants who are greedy for immediate profits, it takes the opportunity to demand whatever it wants, causing Chinese merchants to often enter its valleys without realizing it or being vigilant. This time, the import of Japanese cocoons has been said to have been purchased by various factories and deposited in customs warehouses for use in batches, which is of course purchased by Shanghai merchants. Is it a suicide policy or a goodwill policy? If we do not urgently seek relief and quickly stop it, from then on, our food and clothing will depend on others, and we will be at their mercy. It is unfavorable to Chinese cocoons, and it is also unfavorable to Chinese merchants. Farmers' production is deprived, and merchants' livelihoods are also cut off. I am afraid that drinking poison to quench thirst will not stop until everyone dies. For this reason, I urge you to submit a proposal to find a way to stop it, so that Japanese cocoons will no longer be imported, and to persuade Shanghai merchants to stop ordering them, in order to preserve the inherent production of this country and save the nearly exhausted vitality of farmers and merchants. It is heard that the Municipal Chamber of Commerce is preparing to submit the letter to the current standing committee meeting to discuss the matter.

Declaration of the Citizens' Federation 161

Assistance to Tenants Forcibly Evicted from Qingyun Lane

And Hope That the Landlord Will Wake Up Soon

According to Guowen News Agency, the Shanghai Special District Citizens' Federation issued a declaration yesterday regarding the forced eviction of tenants from Qingyun Lane in Hongkou. According to a letter from the Qingyun Lane Tenants' Federation in Hongkou, the Qingyun Lane property belongs to the New Sassoon Foreign Company. It has been less than thirteen years since it was built, and the existing houses are in good condition and do not need to be rebuilt. At the end of June, they received a notice from the landlord, limited to August 31, forcing them to move. The residents were all shocked when they heard the news. At this time of financial hardship, market depression, high prices, and economic depression, small-scale businesses have reached their limit. The landlord took advantage of the crisis to oppress them, forcing them to move, adding significant losses to the move at a time when they are trying to save themselves. Is this not putting the tenants to death? They repeatedly sent representatives to plead with the landlord to withdraw the order. However, the landlord forgot about righteousness for profit and had no compassion. The residents were forced to have nowhere to go and called for help. The landlord was greedy for profits and leased the Qingyun Lane houses to a certain large company, which had a profound impact on the future of society. The Qingyun Lane houses were rebuilt less than thirteen years ago, and the existing buildings are very solid. There is no need for rebuilding. Now, the landlord New Sassoon Foreign Company disregards business difficulties, ignores public opinion, and rashly forces tenants to move, which is contrary to human nature. It is also clear that someone is instigating from the middle. In order to protect the residents' housing and social security, this federation cannot allow them to be slaughtered. We sincerely hope that the landlord New Sassoon Foreign Company and the rent digger can wake up in time so that a peaceful solution can be reached. Otherwise, this federation will also be involved in the same matter, as it is our duty. This declaration is issued by the Preparatory Committee of the Shanghai Special District Citizens' Federation.

Telegrams from Linru and Neihuang Counties 162

Received by the Henan Relief Association

Zhou Xiaofan, the Shanghai representative of the Henan Relief Association, recently received two telegrams from the provincial government to Xu, the chairman of the Nanjing Relief Committee, and various charitable organizations in Shanghai, which are copied as follows: (1) According to reports from various agencies in Linru, Zhouzhuangzhai in the northeast of the county was captured by bandit leader Cui Yinchuan and others, killing more than 100 people, and taking more than 100 people hostage. Houses, properties, and food were burned and looted. Duzhuang in the west of the county was captured by bandits and is still occupied. On July 15, the west gate of the county town was attacked by bandits again, who burned, killed, looted, and caused countless losses. They took 158 hostages. On the night of July 18, Shilipu, ten miles west of the city, was attacked by bandits who occupied Duzhuang, burned and looted, and took more than 100 hostages. On the 28th, Dangtun in the east of the city was also captured by bandits, and the burning and killing were even more severe, causing even greater losses. Now, the 46th and 47th districts south of the Ru River are full of bandits, and it is difficult to escape or defend. They have no ability to redeem the hostages, and the dying victims are pleading for urgent relief. After investigation, the villages in Linru that were attacked by bandits are destitute and have no food. If no measures are taken to save them, the lives of the people cannot be expected to survive. I implore you to quickly allocate huge sums of money and ask major philanthropists to find ways to provide relief in order to save the survivors. This is our hope. Li Shican, President of the Henan Relief Association, kowtows. (2) According to the report from the Neihuang Relief Sub-Association, Neihuang is the poorest area in the north, and it has been plagued by years of military disasters and banditry, making life difficult for the people. In 1928, there were droughts and locusts, and in 1929, there were droughts, floods, and locusts, making the three disasters even more severe. Tens of thousands of victims abandoned their homes and went east to seek food. This spring, there was another political change, and the allocation of money and conscription of soldiers exhausted everything. They hoped to save their lives with the wheat harvest, but unexpectedly, strong winds and hail caused great damage, so that the wheat ears were all broken and there was no harvest. The young autumn seedlings were all damaged, and the autumn harvest was also hopeless. The survivors are dying and urgently need relief. We implore you to have great compassion and provide relief in order to save the victims. This is our prayer. Li Shican, Chairman of the Henan Relief Association, kowtows. It is heard that after receiving these two telegrams, Representative Zhou went to various charitable organizations to weep and seek relief, and also sent a list of the disasters in various counties to clarify the tragic situation.

Shanghai 165

Commercial Broadcasting Station to be Established

Power Company Actively Preparing for Construction

Focusing on Broadcasting Commercial News

The Shanghai Electric Power Company of the Public Concession recently plans to construct a commercial radio broadcasting station in Shanghai, in order to broadcast commercial news and report market conditions. This plan has already been finalized with specific measures, and the company's board of directors has decided to allocate 100,000 taels of silver to purchase a piece of land for immediate construction. The company has also decided to appoint a key official to personally visit various countries in Europe and America in early October this year to inspect the latest engineering facilities of broadcasting stations, etc., and will order the latest machinery to be transported to China for installation. According to the person in charge of the company, this commercial broadcasting station will be completed and start broadcasting by April next year at the latest. In the future, the broadcast range will not only reach all provinces in China, but also various parts of Japan and the islands of the Pacific Ocean. However, the scope of broadcasting will be limited to commerce. Political news will be completely excluded, with particular attention paid to exchange rates, market prices, and gold standard quotations, in order to make it a purely commercial radio station that can provide prompt news to the business community everywhere.

Wang Zhenmei is from Wuxi, nine years old. Unexpectedly, although the old woman is over sixty, her ferocious nature has not changed. She often used cruel methods such as piercing with needles and scalding with water to abuse her foster daughter. Neighbors who disapproved of her behavior immediately reported it to the China Children's Welfare Association. Yesterday morning, the association sent staff members Wang Guanyi and Zhang Yueru to the destination to investigate the situation. They found that the girl still had injuries on her body, and from the neighbors, they learned that the abuse methods were indeed as previously reported. They originally planned to take the girl away on the spot, but after finding out that her biological mother had come to Shanghai to claim her, they decided to postpone the decision on whether to take her in until her biological mother arrived in Shanghai. Currently, the girl is temporarily living with the Jin Tao Electric Company, a neighbor, so she should not suffer from abuse any longer. As for the punishment that the old woman deserves, it is said that the police have appropriate measures.

Wu Yaoting and Others Reply to Letters from Various Labor Unions 173

More than 20 groups including the Shanghai Xiangsheng Iron Factory Workers' Union, previously issued a declaration stating that they had found that Wu Yaoting and others had set up institutions to privately transport cash out of the country. Wu Yaoting and others yesterday replied separately to the labor unions explaining the misunderstanding, saying: To the Shanghai Xiangsheng Iron Factory Workers' Union, the Pudong Rihua Workers' Union Reorganization Committee, and other groups: Having read the report, the esteemed union's declaration stated that the undersigned and others were taking advantage of the situation to collude with foreign merchants, set up institutions, and privately transport cash out of the country, etc. However, the prohibition of cash exports has long been clearly promulgated by the National Government. The undersigned and others abide by the law and dare not violate it. However, the undersigned and others have been in the gold standard business for many years, buying and selling as a natural act of trading. It is appropriate to store cash when buying, and we operate in compliance with the regulations of the ministry-set exchange. Both the buyer and the seller are bound by the rules, and it is not an illegal act. The esteemed union should know that storing cash and privately transporting it out of the country are two completely different things. Since there is spot gold in Shanghai, how can no one receive it? If storing cash is equated with the crime of privately transporting it out of the country, that is unreasonable. The esteemed union's concern for the national economy and people's livelihood and its ambition to eradicate traitors are admirable. However, this concerns the reputation of the undersigned and others, and we cannot allow false accusations. The esteemed union does not understand the nature of the transaction and cannot arbitrarily slander us with the three characters "Yingshi You". We are deeply surprised and are sending this letter specifically in the hope that the esteemed union will clarify the misunderstanding and thoroughly investigate to clarify the truth. Awaiting your reply, respectfully, Wu Yaoting and Yu Shouzheng. Also, Wu Peichu's reply to the various labor unions states: (Omitted above) Having read the report, the esteemed union stated that the undersigned was taking advantage of the situation to privately transport cash out of the country, etc. As the undersigned has always worked in the bank, I have no knowledge of matters outside of my duties. I am surprised to be listed. I hope that the esteemed union will thoroughly investigate to clarify the truth. Respectfully, Wu Peichu.

News from Trade Associations 174

Copper and Tin Industry: The Shanghai Copper and Tin Trade Association has been ordered to reorganize. Preparations have been completed, and the inaugural meeting was convened at the regular meeting room of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday. The meeting began at 2:15, with rituals as usual. Chairman Yu Futang reported on the merger and reorganization of the guild hall and the association, stating: Our industry established a guild hall in the late Qing Dynasty, with directors presiding over everything. After the revolution, a council was produced by the members. In the fifth year of the Republic of China, the association was established, and the General Chamber of Commerce was requested to report to the Ministry for registration. In the sixth year, funds were raised to rebuild the old site, so the association affairs could gradually develop. Unexpectedly, in the winter of the thirteenth year, it was occupied by Zhang Yunming's army, and it suffered greatly. The bad example has been set, and troops are still borrowing residence to this day, resulting in no fixed address, which is a great regret. Since being ordered to merge and reorganize into a trade association, after several months of preparation, it can be announced today. We are very honored that the Municipal Party Department and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau sent personnel to attend for guidance and supervision. I hope that the fellow tradesmen present will work together, unite as one, relieve their own suffering, and enthusiastically create wealth for society, so as not to disappoint the enthusiasm of the representatives present. Next, the charter, totaling twenty-four articles, was discussed, and there were no objections from the public, and it was passed. Next, the executive committee members were elected by ballot. As a result, Tian Hexiang, Yu Futang, Yi Nanzhen, Feng Yongmei, Xia Juntang, Huang Chunquan, Yi Yaochang, Yi Qichang, Jin Keqing, Xiao Erjun, and Wang Lianfang were elected. They were immediately sworn into office. Next, a representative from the Citizen Training Association gave a training speech. The meeting adjourned at five o'clock.

Candle Industry: The Municipal Candle Industry Association believes that fellow traders add gifts every festival, which has become a custom. It is difficult to maintain the current situation without active rectification. Yesterday, all fellow traders were invited to a meeting to discuss the results: (1) The old habit of giving gifts in this industry is the beginning of price chaos, and it should be banned to facilitate rectification. (2) The case of member Sanhecheng Firm resisting payment of association fees has been dealt with according to law by the superior association, and it has been decided that they should still pay fees in accordance with the regulations. If the firm continues to be contemptuous, it will be reported to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the judicial authorities for legal punishment. The meeting adjourned after discussion.

Hotel Industry: The Shanghai Hotel Industry Association of Hele Lane, Fuzhou Road, sent its 80th official letter yesterday to the Shanghai Public Concession Taxpayers' Association, stating: I hereby report that our association members, including Yao Shengsan of the Southern Hotel and more than ten other hotels, have written letters stating that the number of hotels in Shanghai's industry was not as numerous as it is today ten years ago. In business, supply and demand were originally commensurate, so in addition to expenses, there was always some surplus. In recent years, due to the investment of investors who do not understand the social and economic organization, there has been an oversupply of hotels, and business has plummeted. Not only can most hotels' businesses not maintain expenses, but the losses are increasing year by year after the annual settlement. I am afraid that if this continues and no remedy is sought, and the pain of increased rent, increased staff salaries, increased tax burdens, and unstable times is added, they will inevitably close down. Such consequences are unimaginable. The members felt the danger and could not remain silent. Therefore, they are writing to request that you promptly send a letter to the Taxpayers' Association, which will then send a letter to the Public Works Department, urging them to restrict the increase in the number of hotels. If a hotel comes to apply for a license, it should be rejected in order to leave a bit of business for hotel merchants, preserve their capital, and avoid mass bankruptcy and social panic. The situation is so important. I hereby request that your association review and approve this proposal, or send a letter to the board of directors of the Public Works Department, requesting them to consider the decline in hotel business and the danger of increasing numbers within the boundary, approve the restriction of hotels from increasing from today, and not issue licenses indiscriminately again, in order to maintain the business of the original hotels within the boundary, fulfill the obligation of taxpayers, and ensure the economic stability of society.
